free cash flow* $0.4B, +$0.2B</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:3pt"><font><br></font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10.5pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">BOSTON &#8212; July&#160;25, 2023 &#8212; GE (NYSE&#58;GE) announced results today for the second quarter ending June 30, 2023. </font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10.5pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">GE Chairman and CEO and GE Aerospace CEO H. Lawrence Culp, Jr. said, &#34;GE's second-quarter performance was strong, building on our first-quarter momentum and marking a solid first half of the year. Orders and revenue grew double digits, led by robust services growth across our portfolio, increased demand at GE Aerospace and record Renewable Energy orders. Today, we are raising our full-year guidance as market strength and the lean transformation within our more focused businesses drive significant profit and cash improvement across GE.&#8221;</font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10.5pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Culp continued, &#34;GE Aerospace is growing rapidly, executing on the ramp for customers and building services strength, while GE Vernova advances toward its spin-off as Renewable Energy improves and Power continues to deliver. Each business has its own critical mission and focus. We&#8217;re increasingly operating as GE Aerospace and GE Vernova as we prepare to launch these two independent companies sometime in early 2024.&#8221;</font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10.5pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">The company continued to execute during the quarter&#58;</font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10.5pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%">GE Aerospace</font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div style="padding-left:22.5pt;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10.5pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">&#8226;</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Arial',sans-serif;font-size:10.5pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%;padding-left:14.33pt">Delivered double-digit growth in orders, revenue, and operating profit year-over-year driven by commercial momentum and strength in services. Commercial Engines &#38; Services improved LEAP output by 85% year-over-year and Commercial Services grew 31%. Defense orders more than doubled, and the team improved unit output by 74% year-over-year. </font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div style="padding-left:22.5pt;text-indent:-18pt"><font Commercial Services and Defense. Revenues of $7.9 billion grew 28% on a reported and organic* basis, with equipment growing at double the rate of services. Both LEAP and Defense engine deliveries grew in the quarter. Commercial Services grew with strong external spare part sales and higher internal shop visits. Segment margin of 18.8% expanded by 10 basis points on a reported basis and contracted (30) basis points organically*. Volume, pricing net of inflation, and productivity were offset by unfavorable mix, increased investments, and the non-repeat of positive contract margin adjustments last year.
